Indicator 15.2.1: Progress towards sustainable forest management

This comparison shows additions and deletions to metadata files in detailed format. This view may be helpful when precisely updating translations.

Only updates made by the World Bank Translation Project Team are shown. The original source file for all English metadata files is the UNSD SDG Metadata Repository.

Last update: March 2019

  <p>The forest area change direction is determined by examining the value of the forest area change rate for the most recent period, a negative value indicate a loss of forest area, a zero value means that forest area is stable and a positive value means that forest area has increased. The change in forest area loss rate is based on a comparison of the current forest area net change rate with the <u>baseline forest area net change rate for the period 2010-2015.</u></p>
61
  <p><u>Comments:</u></p>
62
  <p>This traffic light takes into consideration both the direction of forest area change (if forest area increases or decreases) as well as changes in the rate of forest area loss &#x2013; the latter important in order to indicate progress among countries that are losing forest area but manage to reduce the loss rate. </p>
63
  <p>For annual reporting, FAO can provide countries with imputed values based on previous trends that they can use in case they don&#x2019;t have new/updated information. The baseline should be updated every 5 years, so in 2020 a new baseline is calculated. Also, at country level, if a country gets new information and updates the historical time series, the baseline for the country will be recalculated, respecting the 2010-2015 period.</p>

+ <h1>Annex 1 &#x2013; Terms and Definitions <sup><a href="#footnote-1" id="footnote-ref-1">[1]</a></sup> </h1>
5
  <p><strong><em>FOREST</em></strong></p>
6
  <p>Land spanning more than 0.5 hectares with trees higher than 5 meters and a canopy cover of more than 10 percent, or trees able to reach these thresholds <em>in situ</em>. It does not include land that is predominantly under agricultural or urban land use<strong>. </strong></p>

52
  <p>The forest area change direction is determined by examining the value of the forest area change rate for the most recent period, a negative value indicate a loss of forest area, a zero value means that forest area is stable and a positive value means that forest area has increased. The change in forest area loss rate is based on a comparison of the current forest area net change rate with the <u>baseline forest area net change rate for the period 2010-2015.</u></p>
53
  <p><u>Comments:</u></p>
54
  <p>This traffic light takes into consideration both the direction of forest area change (if forest area increases or decreases) as well as changes in the rate of forest area loss &#x2013; the latter important in order to indicate progress among countries that are losing forest area but manage to reduce the loss rate. </p>
55
  <p>For annual reporting, FAO can provide countries with imputed values based on previous trends that they can use in case they don&#x2019;t have new/updated information. The baseline should be updated every 5 years, so in 2020 a new baseline is calculated. Also, at country level, if a country gets new information and updates the historical time series, the baseline for the country will be recalculated, respecting the 2010-2015 period.</p>
59
  <p><u>Method of estimation:</u> Biomass stock in forest (tonnes) / forest area (ha)</p>
60
  <p><u>Translation to dashboard/traffic light:</u></p>
61
  <p>The indicator value for the latest reporting year is compared with the indicator value for previous reporting year for assessment of continuity of progress since last report.</p>
62
  <p>The ratio (r) between the current indicator value and the previously reported value is calculated; r&gt;1 means an increase in stock per hectare, r&lt;1 means a decrease while 1 indicates no change. A narrow interval for r has been established to indicate a stable condition, and traffic-light colors are assigned as follows:</p>
63

67
  <p><u>Method of estimation:</u> Forest area within legally established protected areas / forest area 2015 * 100</p>
68
  <p><u>Translation to dashboard/traffic light:</u></p>
69
  <p>The indicator value for latest reporting year is compared the indicator value for previous reporting year for assessment of continuity of progress since last report.</p>
70
  <p>The ratio (r) between the current indicator value and the previously reported value is calculated; r&gt;1 means an increase in forest area within protected areas, r&lt;1 means a decrease while 1 indicates no change. A narrow interval for r has been established to indicate a stable condition, and traffic-light colors are assigned as follows:</p>
71

  <p>Using forest area in 2015 as denominator for estimating this indicator ensures that the time series of percentages reflect real changes in the forest area within legally established protected areas and is not affected by changes (losses or gains) in total forest area. </p>

  <p><strong><em>Sub-indicator 4 &#x2013; Proportion of forest area under a long-term forest management plan.</em></strong></p>
75
  <p><u>Unit</u>: Percent</p>
76
  <p><u>Reference year:</u> Latest reporting year</p>
77
  <p><u>Method of estimation:</u> Forest area under a long term forest management plan / forest area 2015 * 100</p>
78
  <p><u>Translation to dashboard/traffic light: </u>The indicator value for latest reporting year is compared with the indicator value for previous reporting year for assessment of continuity of progress since last report.</p>
79
  <p>The ratio (r) between the current indicator value and the previously reported value is calculated; r&gt;1 means an increase in areas under forest management plan, r&lt;1 means a decrease while 1 indicates no change. A narrow interval for r has been established to indicate a stable condition, and traffic-light colors are assigned as follows:</p>

  <p>Using forest area in 2015 as denominator for estimating this indicator ensures that the time series of percentages reflect real changes in the forest area under forest management plan and is not affected by changes (losses or gains) in total forest area. </p>

  <p><strong><em>Sub-indicator 5 &#x2013; Forest area under an independently verified forest management certification scheme.</em></strong></p>
84
  <p><u>Unit</u>: Thousand hectares</p>
86
  <p><u>Method of estimation:</u> Data is collected directly from the databases of each certification scheme and provided to countries for validation.</p>
87
  <p><u>Translation to dashboard/traffic light: </u>The indicator value for latest reporting year is compared with the indicator value for previous reporting year for assessment of continuity of progress since last report.</p>
88
  <p>The ratio (r) between the current indicator value and the previously reported value is calculated; r&gt;1 means an increase in areas under an independent forest management certification scheme, r&lt;1 means a decrease while 1 indicates no change. A</p>
89
  <p>small interval for r has been established to indicate a stable condition, and traffic-light colors are assigned as follows:</p>

  <p>Using June 30 as the date for reporting, allows for the certification bodies to have their databases updated so they can provide information to FAO by end of the year, and then be included in the annual reporting to SDG in the beginning of the following year.</p><div class="footnotes"><div><sup class="footnote-number" id="footnote-1">1</sup><p> Global Forest Resources Assessment 2015 &#x2013; Terms and Definitions. <a href="http://www.fao.org/docrep/017/ap862e/ap862e00.pdf">http://www.fao.org/docrep/017/ap862e/ap862e00.pdf</a> <a href="#footnote-ref-1">&#x2191;</a></p></div></div>
